Topic 0: Introduction & Glossary

導論與術語 | p1-p6

PDA Points to Consider No. 1 | p1 – p6 | 127 pages total

本章學習目標

  • 理解 PDA PtC-1 的歷史沿革（2003 → 2015/16 → 2023），以及 2022 EU Annex 1 如何觸發本次修訂
  • 掌握指導本文件的五大原則，並能解釋每一原則對 CDMO 日常決策的實務意涵
  • 熟悉 Glossary 中每個術語的精確定義，辨別易混淆的相似詞（如 At-Rest vs. In-Operations，Action Limit vs. Alert Limit）
  • 建立「無菌保證 (Sterility Assurance) 優先於一切」的決策階層思維框架
0.1 Introduction — Background & Five Guiding Principles

原文內容 Original Text

Points to Consider No. 1: Aseptic Processing (Revised 2023) offers PDA's thoughts and does not represent a standard or regulatory guidance.

PDA first issued Points to Consider for Aseptic Processing in 2003. To address the impact of the knowledge gained in the intervening years, PDA assembled a task force of subject-matter experts from industry to revise this report. Published in 2015 and 2016, Points to Consider for Aseptic Processing parts 1 and 2 provided positions on current topics, best practices, and areas of clarification important to the manufacture of quality sterile products.

NOTE: The topics discussed in the 2015 and 2016 Points to Consider documents are superseded by this revision.

With technology and regulatory advancements, specifically the issuance of the revised European GMP Annex 1: Manufacture of Sterile Medicinal Products (EU Annex 1) in August 2022, another update of this document was undertaken. This revision reflects current industry best practices and scientific positions as well as regulatory expectations. Where there may be a divergence between recommendations in this Points to Consider document and a regulatory position, that divergence is noted.

Many of the topics included in the 2015 Points to Consider resulted from discussion and input from PDA members at conferences and meetings. These topics were reviewed considering the advancements made in the past decade and, where applicable, this report has been revised based on similar inputs. While the current revision maintains the original organization of topics into categories, topics that had been discussed separately in Parts 1 and 2 have been combined into a single document. Each topic discussion begins with a problem statement in the form of a question about issues or points needing clarification on that specific topic. Recommendations from the PDA task force are then presented as an answer to the question. The rationale and references for each recommendation follow.

This document provides points to consider on topics related to the physical environment in which aseptic processing is conducted, monitoring of that environment, cleanroom personnel, material transfer, aseptic process simulation and validation, "modern" blow-fill-seal technology, cleaning, disinfection and sterilization, and critical utilities. It also includes points to consider on aspects of filter-integrity testing and water-for-injection (WFI) preparation.

The recommendations presented in this Points to Consider document are based on five guiding and linked principles for improvement in sterile health care products:

1 Scientifically sound, risk-based approaches should be used to obtain information needed to make decisions related to the evaluation, design, qualification, operation, and monitoring of sterile-product manufacturing processes. Risk- and science-based approaches should be used as well to develop and implement control strategies and acceptance criteria designed to ensure the establishment and maintenance of manufacturing conditions that affect the sterility of products. Sterile drug-product manufacturing processes and testing requirements should have a basis in and relevance to risks to product quality and patient safety. Similar principles and considerations may also apply to non-sterile drug products. Risk management and assessment methods should be developed not only to identify risks, but also to allow the improvement of processes and control strategies.
2 Where feasible, the use of newer technologies should be considered to mitigate or reduce risks to product quality identified in manufacturing processes and operations. Companies involved in the manufacture of sterile drug products should be encouraged to identify and consider the use of modern technologies, and regulatory guidance should enable this by presenting expectations that encourage the use of these technologies. Technologies and facility, equipment, and process designs that protect products and product-contact surfaces from personnel and environmental contact and that provide more reliable and useful information are particularly beneficial to reducing the risk of microbiological contamination during aseptic processing.
3 The effectiveness of certain traditional testing and monitoring methods used as control strategies should be reevaluated. As technology has been introduced and knowledge has been acquired, the usefulness and value of testing procedures have changed. Testing and monitoring should be designed and performed, and the results should be evaluated, based on scientific value, risk to product quality, patient safety, and usefulness in determining process control. Where testing and monitoring approaches and methods no longer meet current needs or are not optimal, their replacement or modification should be considered. The use of outdated testing and monitoring methods has the potential to increase risk, provide a false sense of control, prove ineffective, and deploy resources in a manner that may not be efficient or optimal, thus detracting from the development and use of more effective testing and monitoring approaches.
4 New product/container presentations, therapies, and technologies present challenges to existing methods for the development, manufacture, validation, and testing of sterile products. To meet these challenges, an emphasis on thorough technical and process understanding, science, and risk will become important in designing effective means to ensure product quality. Companies should be encouraged to seek out the most effective means rather than try to fit traditional methods to these new products, technologies, and therapies.
5 When scientific approaches are similar and agreed upon, global health authority requirements and guidance should be consistent in technical language and definition. Harmonized technical and regulatory language, where possible, should be consistent with approaches presented in other similar guidance documents. This practice should promote clarity of global regulatory expectations and reduce the risk of misunderstanding and redundant efforts.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — PDA PtC-1 是什麼？為什麼重要？

Points to Consider (PtC，考量要點) 是 PDA 出版的一種特殊文件類型，介於技術報告（Technical Report）與法規指引之間。它不具法規約束力，但代表業界最佳智識共識，常被 FDA 與 EMA 稽查員引用作為期望水準的參考依據。

PtC-1 專注於無菌加工 (Aseptic Processing)，是整個 PDA 文獻體系中關於無菌環境管控、人員、APS 模擬、BFS 技術、清潔消毒的最權威單一文件。對 CDMO 而言，這份文件等同於「客戶稽核的教科書」。

比喻說明 — 文件版本演進的比喻

想像 PtC-1 是一本「廚房衛生操作手冊」：

  • 2003 年版：基礎版，教你洗手與刀具消毒
  • 2015/2016 年版：加入新式不鏽鋼廚具與空氣過濾設備的指引，分上下冊
  • 2023 年版（本版）：合併上下冊，並全面對齊 2022 年發布的「全球最嚴格廚房衛生法規」（EU Annex 1）——不只更新設備章節，連人員資格、消毒劑輪換等細節全部重寫

重點：舊版（2015/16）已被本版完全取代。如果你的 SOP 還引用 2015 年 PtC-1，現在必須更新。

重點提示 — 2022 EU Annex 1 的衝擊

2022 年 8 月，歐盟發布重新修訂的 GMP Annex 1，全長 58 頁（前版僅 16 頁），新增大量要求：

  • 強制要求 Contamination Control Strategy (CCS，污染控制策略) 作為系統性文件
  • Isolator 與 RABS 明確區分，並提升 RABS 要求等級
  • BFS 技術納入 "modern technology" 框架
  • APS 媒體填充要求更嚴格

正因 Annex 1 如此重大，PDA 才緊急於 2023 年更新 PtC-1，確保兩者技術立場相符。每當 Annex 1 與 PtC-1 有分歧，本文件會明確標注——這個設計對 CDMO 特別寶貴，因為你的客戶可能同時受 FDA 與 EMA 管轄。

五大原則解析（CDMO 視角）

原則 1 — 科學/風險導向：不能只依賴「傳統做法就這樣」，每個決策（環境監控頻率、APS 挑戰數量）都要有科學根據與風險評估支撐。對 CDMO：當客戶要求比 GMP 更嚴的標準時，用風險評估說明你現有標準已足夠或確實需要提升。

原則 2 — 採用新技術：法規鼓勵使用 Isolator、RABS、一次性系統等新技術，不應因「稽查官不熟悉」而保守。CDMO 的競爭優勢之一就是率先導入新技術。

原則 3 — 重新評估傳統方法：某些傳統測試（如固定頻率的手動 settle plates）可能已過時，應以更科學的方式取代。這是本版最具突破性的立場之一。

原則 4 — 新療法/新技術的挑戰：mRNA 疫苗、CAR-T 細胞治療等新型態產品，無法套用傳統無菌加工框架，必須重新設計管控策略。

原則 5 — 全球法規一致性：FDA、EMA、PIC/S 技術語言的統一，減少 CDMO 在多地區申請時重複努力。

實務應用 — CDMO 的 PtC-1 使用場景

場景 1：客戶稽核準備
客戶品保問："你們的環境監測計畫依據哪份指引？"
回答："依據 FDA Aseptic Guidance (2004)、EU Annex 1 (2022) 及 PDA PtC-1 (2023 修訂版)，三者相互對照，差異處均有書面說明。"

場景 2：SOP 審查
稽核員發現你的 SOP 引用 "PDA PtC for Aseptic Processing (2016)"——應立即更新為 2023 年版，並說明兩版差異評估已完成。

場景 3：技術評估新技術
評估是否導入 Isolator 時，引用原則 2 作為技術決策依據，並透過 QRM 評估風險降低的程度，向客戶展示投資價值。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. PDA PtC-1 與 FDA Aseptic Guidance 的法規位階有何不同？在稽查中各自扮演什麼角色？
  2. 為什麼 2022 EU Annex 1 的發布會促使 PDA 在 2023 年修訂 PtC-1？這說明了 PDA 文件與法規的什麼關係？
  3. 五大原則中，哪一個原則最能支持你考慮將手動 settle plates 改為持續粒子計數器？請說明理由。
0.2 Glossary — Defined Terms

原文內容 Original Text

Definitions have been provided to help clarify the concepts discussed in this document. While some of the definitions vary among companies, the definitions described below are consistent for use within this Points to Consider document. Where a definition is based on another published source, the source is cited.

Aborted Run

Aseptic process simulation run that begins and is then stopped and not filled to completion.

Action Limit

An established relevant measure (e.g., microbial, or airborne particle limits) that, when exceeded, should trigger appropriate investigation and corrective action based on the investigation.

NOTE: In a prior version of this document, this term was called "Action Level."
Advanced Aseptic Processing Personnel Qualification

A defined and documented procedure for determining the criteria by which personnel are permitted to enter and perform higher-risk and complex activities, under less supervision, in the aseptic processing area during commercial operations. (See Section IV, Topic B.)

Air Shroud

A physical enclosure for a blow-fill-seal (BFS) machine that contains or surrounds the filling zone. It is typically supplied by sterile filtered or Grade A quality air. The air shroud should be sterilized or decontaminated to maintain Grade A conditions.

Air Visualization Studies / Airflow Visualization Studies

Tests using a visible medium (e.g., smoke or vaporized liquid nitrogen) simulating the properties of air flow, designed to indicate the direction and disruption of air flow. Sometimes referred to as 'smoke studies'.

Aseptic Preparation / Processing

The handling of sterile product, containers and/or devices in a controlled environment in which the air supply, materials and personnel are regulated to prevent microbial, endotoxin/pyrogen and particle contamination.

Aseptic Process Simulation (APS)

A means for establishing the capability of an aseptic process as performed using a growth medium.

At-Rest

The condition whereby the installation of all the utilities is complete including any functioning HVAC, with the main manufacturing equipment installed as specified but not operating and without personnel present in the room.

Blow-Fill-Seal (BFS) Process

The BFS machine, including the parison extrusion, parison transport (if applicable), container filling and final sealing operations.

NOTE: Some companies refer to this process as "Form-Fill-Seal" (FFS). However, EU Annex 1 defines Form-Fill-Seal as an automated filling process, typically used for terminally sterilised products, which constructs the primary container out of a continuous flat roll of packaging film while simultaneously filling and sealing in a continuous process.
Corrective and Preventive Actions (CAPA)

Actions to eliminate the cause of a detected nonconformity or other undesirable situation.

NOTE: Corrective actions are taken to prevent recurrence, whereas preventive actions are taken to prevent occurrence.
Cleaning Agents

The solution or solvent used in the washing step of a cleaning process. Examples of cleaning agents are water, organic solvent, commodity chemical diluted in water, and formulated detergent diluted in water.

Closed Parison (Rotary or Reciprocating Machines)

BFS machines that use a fill system enclosed in the continuous parison. Containers are closed in such a way as to not expose the parison interior or fill zone to the environment.

Contamination Control Strategy (CCS)

A planned set of controls for microorganisms, endotoxin/pyrogen and particles, derived from current product and process understanding that assures process performance and product quality. The controls can include parameters and attributes related to active substance, excipient and drug product materials and components, facility and equipment operating conditions, in-process controls, finished product specifications, and the associated methods and frequency of monitoring and control.

Critical Surface

A surface within a critical zone that may come in direct contact with sterilized products, containers, or closures.

Critical Zone

A location within the aseptic processing area in which product and critical surfaces are exposed to the environment.

NOTE: This term was previously referred to as "Critical Area."
Disinfectant

A chemical or physical agent that reduces, destroys, or eliminates vegetative forms of harmful microorganisms, but not spores.

Disqualification of Aseptic Processing Personnel

A defined and documented procedure for determining the criteria by which previously qualified aseptic processing personnel are no longer permitted to enter and perform higher-risk and complex activities in the aseptic processing area during commercial operations. (See Section IV, Topic B.)

Environmental Monitoring (EM)

Describes the processes and activities that need to take place to characterize and monitor the quality of the environment.

First Air

Refers to filtered air that has not been interrupted prior to contacting exposed product and product contact surfaces with the potential to add contamination to the air prior to reaching the critical zone.

Grade A Air Supply

Air which is passed through a filter qualified as capable of producing grade A total particle quality air, but where there is no requirement to perform continuous total particle monitoring or meet grade A viable monitoring limits. Specifically used for the protection of fully stoppered vials where the cap has not yet been crimped.

Good Manufacturing Practice (GMP)

Best practices in manufacturing of pharmaceuticals or biopharmaceuticals. From a regulatory standpoint, GMPs are regarded as the minimum current good manufacturing practice for methods to be used in, and the facilities or controls to be used for, the manufacture, processing, packaging, or holding of a drug to assure that such drug meets the requirements of safety, identity, and strength and meets the quality and purity characteristics that it purports or is represented to possess.

High-Efficiency Particulate Air (HEPA) Filter

High efficiency particulate air filter with minimum 0.3 µm particle retaining efficiency of 99.97 percent.

In-Operations

Condition where the installation of the cleanroom is complete, the HVAC system fully operational, equipment installed and functioning in the manufacturer's defined operating mode with the maximum number of personnel present performing or simulating routine operational work.

Invalid Run

Aseptic processing simulation run that was filled to completion and then invalidated.

Isolator

A contained, decontaminated environment meeting Grade A/ISO 5 conditions used for aseptic process manufacturing that provides an uncompromised, continuous isolation of its interior from the external environment. Once decontaminated by a validated cycle, an isolator prevents the microbiological contamination of sterile products and product contact surfaces of the interior by enclosures and the supply of continuous, controlled overpressure of HEPA-filtered air.

Closed isolator systems exclude external contamination from the isolator's interior by accomplishing material transfer via aseptic connection to auxiliary equipment, rather than using openings to the surrounding environment. Closed systems remain sealed throughout operations.

Open isolator systems are designed to allow for the continuous or semi-continuous ingress and/or egress of materials during operations through one or more openings. Openings are engineered (e.g., using continuous overpressure) to exclude the entry of external contamination into the isolator.

Initial Aseptic Processing Personnel Qualification

A defined and documented procedure for determining the criteria by which personnel are permitted to enter and perform certain low-risk and less complex activities, under direct supervision, in the aseptic processing area during commercial operations. (See Section IV, Topic B.)

Ongoing Aseptic Processing Personnel Assessment

A defined and documented procedure for determining the criteria by which the performance of personnel, deemed as qualified to enter and perform activities in the aseptic processing area during commercial operations, is assessed on a prescribed, periodic basis. (See Section IV, Topic B.)

Open Parison (Shuttle Machines)

Blow-fill-seal machines where the parison is cut from the extruder and the open parison is contained in the mold during transport to the critical fill zone.

Requalification of Aseptic Processing Personnel following Disqualification

A defined and documented procedure for determining the criteria by which previously disqualified aseptic processing personnel are again permitted to enter and perform activities in the aseptic processing area during commercial operations. (See Section IV, Topic B.)

Restricted Access Barrier System (RABS)

An area that includes one or more critical work areas that is fully or partially enclosed with ridged or semi-rigid walls, which restricts the access of aseptic processing personnel, via fixed gloves, to the critical work area during aseptic operations.

Sanitizers

A compound that will reduce the number of vegetative microorganisms to a safe level as determined by public health requirements. Normally, a reduction of 103 in vegetative microorganisms is obtained.

Total Particulate

Refers to what is often termed "nonviable particles," which, in fact, are measures of both viable and nonviable particulates.

References

  1. European Commission. Annex 1: Manufacture of Sterile Medicinal Products, EudraLex – Volume 4 – EU Guidelines for Good Manufacturing Practice for Medicinal Products for Human and Veterinary Use; European Commission: Brussels, 2022.
  2. Parenteral Drug Association, Inc. Points to Consider for the Aseptic Processing of Sterile Pharmaceutical Products in Isolators; PDA, Bethesda, Md., 2020.
  3. U.S. Food and Drug Administration. Guidance for Industry: Sterile Drug Products Produced by Aseptic Processing—Current Good Manufacturing Practice; U.S. Department of Health and Human Services: Rockville, Md., 2004.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

為什麼 Glossary 如此重要？

GMP 文件中的術語定義不是裝飾，而是法規語言的基礎。一旦術語定義不同，可能導致：

  • 法規分歧：FDA 與 EMA 對同一概念的定義微妙差異，影響驗證策略
  • 內部誤解：工廠操作員、QA、客戶對 "Action Limit" 與 "Alert Limit" 的混用
  • 稽查缺失：稽查員發現你的 SOP 使用了被取代的舊術語（如 "Action Level" → "Action Limit"；"Critical Area" → "Critical Zone"）

PtC-1 的 Glossary 已與 2022 EU Annex 1 對齊，請務必以此版本為準更新你的 SOP 術語。

比喻說明 — At-Rest vs. In-Operations

把無塵室想像成一間手術室：

  • At-Rest（靜態）：手術室清潔完畢、設備就位、空調運轉，但手術團隊尚未進入——就像手術前的環境檢測狀態
  • In-Operations（動態）：手術正在進行，醫護人員全員到位、最大人數活動中——這才是真正代表生產條件的狀態

GMP 要求兩種狀態都要達標，但 In-Operations 的粒子計數要求更嚴格，因為人員活動會產生污染。絕不可只測 At-Rest 然後宣稱符合動態標準。

重點提示 — 人員資格的三層架構

PtC-1 首次在 Glossary 層級明確定義人員資格的三個階段，這是本版的重要創新：

階段 英文術語 對應活動 監督強度
初始資格 Initial Qualification 低風險、簡單操作 直接監督
進階資格 Advanced Qualification 高風險、複雜操作 較少監督
持續評估 Ongoing Assessment 定期重新評估 週期性

此外還有 Disqualification（取消資格） 與 Requalification（重新資格） 的程序，形成完整的人員管控閉環。CDMO 應建立對應的 SOP 與資格矩陣。

易混淆術語對比解析

Disinfectant（消毒劑）vs. Sanitizer（衛生劑）：

  • Disinfectant：殺滅植物型微生物，但不包括孢子
  • Sanitizer：將植物型微生物降至安全水準（通常 10³ 降低），標準比消毒劑更低
  • GMP 無菌區域通常使用 Disinfectant，而非僅 Sanitizer

Aborted Run vs. Invalid Run（APS 相關）：

  • Aborted Run：開始後中止，未完成充填——需調查為何中止，通常需要重新執行
  • Invalid Run：充填完成後才被認定無效——需有充分的科學論據支持無效化，否則必須視為失敗
  • 兩者的處理程序完全不同，混淆可能導致重大稽查缺失

Critical Zone vs. Critical Surface：

  • Critical Zone（關鍵區域）：產品暴露的空間位置
  • Critical Surface（關鍵表面）：Critical Zone 內可能直接接觸產品/容器/封蓋的表面
  • Critical Surface 一定在 Critical Zone 內，但 Critical Zone 不是每個點都是 Critical Surface

BFS 術語解析 — Parison 類型的無菌意義

BFS（Blow-Fill-Seal，吹製-充填-封口）製程中，parison（型坯）的設計直接影響無菌保證：

  • Closed Parison（密閉型坯）：充填系統完全包覆在連續型坯內，充填區不暴露於環境——污染風險較低，但機器設計更複雜
  • Open Parison（開放型坯）：型坯切斷後在模具中傳送至充填區，型坯內部短暫暴露——需要 Air Shroud 提供 Grade A 保護

Air Shroud（氣流罩）是 Open Parison 設計中的關鍵污染控制元件，必須使用無菌過濾或 Grade A 品質的空氣，並定期消毒/去污染。

First Air 概念 — 無菌充填的核心原理

First Air（初始氣流）是 HEPA 過濾器吹出後、尚未受任何障礙物干擾的空氣。這是 Grade A 保護最純淨的狀態。

實務原則：產品暴露部位（開口容器、填針）必須始終沐浴在 First Air 中。任何障礙物（操作員的手、零件、工具托盤）一旦介於 HEPA 與產品之間，First Air 就被打斷，污染風險立即上升。

這也是為何無菌操作員手部動作必須嚴格訓練的根本原因，也是 Airflow Visualization Study（氣流可視化研究）必須評估的核心項目。

Total Particulate — 術語澄清

"Total Particulate" ≠ "非活性粒子（Nonviable Particles）"

Total Particulate 的測量值包含：
  ├── Viable Particles（活性粒子，含微生物）
  └── Nonviable Particles（非活性粒子）

環境監控（EM）常見粒子計數器量測的是：
  → 所有 ≥0.5 µm 與 ≥5.0 µm 粒子的總和
  → 即 Total Particulate，而非單純 Nonviable

重要意涵：即使粒子計數超標，
也不能推論一定有微生物污染；
反之，即使粒子計數合格，
也不能完全排除微生物風險。
兩種監控方式互補，不能相互取代。

重點提示 — CCS 是系統性架構，不是清單

Contamination Control Strategy (CCS，污染控制策略) 的定義強調幾個關鍵詞：

  • "Planned set of controls"：必須是系統性、有計畫的控制組合，不是拼湊的清單
  • "Derived from current product and process understanding"：必須基於對產品與製程的現況理解，隨新知識動態更新
  • "Assures process performance AND product quality"：同時保證製程表現與產品品質，缺一不可

EU Annex 1 要求 CCS 作為正式文件存在。對 CDMO，CCS 應是客戶技術協議 (Quality Agreement) 中的核心附件之一，也是無菌設施稽查的重點審查對象。

實務應用 — Isolator vs. RABS 在 CDMO 的選擇決策

根據 Glossary 定義，兩者的核心差異在「隔離的完整性」：

  • Isolator：「uncompromised, continuous isolation」——太空站，外部與內部完全隔絕，去污染週期後內部被視為獨立無菌空間，APS 失敗風險極低
  • RABS：「restricts access via fixed gloves」——仍是有限制進入的開放架構，需要背景 Grade B 潔淨室，人員干預管控要求高

決策框架（依 PROMPT.md 決策階層）：

無菌保證要求 (APS Pass Rate, Product Sterility Risk)
▼
產品 CQAs（熱敏感性、暴露時間窗口、批量大小）
▼
商業考量（投資金額、廠房空間、客戶偏好）

只有在前兩層需求滿足後，才應考慮商業可行性。商業壓力不能倒推決定 Isolator 或 RABS 的選擇。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 你的工廠 SOP 記載清潔步驟使用「消毒劑輪換」，但某同事認為只要使用 Sanitizer 就夠了。請根據 PtC-1 Glossary 的定義，說明兩者差異，以及無菌區域應使用哪一種？
  2. APS 執行過程中，充填機因警報而暫停，操作員排除故障後繼續完成充填，最終培養結果全陰性。這是 Aborted Run 還是一般的 APS 完成？該如何處理？
  3. 如果你的 Grade B 背景室粒子計數合格，是否可以推論 Grade A 工作區也必然合格？請根據 At-Rest / In-Operations 的定義說明。
  4. CCS 文件中，你打算只列舉 EM 監控計畫與清潔 SOP。稽查員可能指出什麼缺口？根據 CCS 的完整定義，還應涵蓋哪些要素？

本節重點回顧 Section Summary

  • 歷史沿革：PtC-1 歷經 2003 → 2015/16 → 2023 三次演進；2023 版由 EU Annex 1 (2022) 觸發，完全取代前兩版，並將分冊合一
  • 五大原則：科學/風險導向、採用新技術、重新評估傳統測試、因應新療法挑戰、全球法規語言一致性——這五個原則貫穿 PtC-1 全文所有建議的邏輯基礎
  • 關鍵術語辨析：Action Limit（非 Level）、Critical Zone（非 Area）、Aborted vs. Invalid Run、At-Rest vs. In-Operations、Disinfectant vs. Sanitizer、Total Particulate（含活性粒子）
  • 人員資格框架：Initial → Advanced Qualification → Ongoing Assessment → Disqualification → Requalification，形成完整閉環，CDMO 必須建立對應 SOP
  • CCS 是系統性文件：EU Annex 1 要求正式 CCS，涵蓋原料、設施、設備、製程參數、EM、成品規格等全面控制——不只是 EM 計畫
  • 決策階層不動搖：無菌保證 > 產品 CQAs > 商業考量，此優先順序在 PtC-1 每一章節的建議背後都得到體現
1a

Topic 1a: I. Physical Environment (A-H): Airflow, HEPA, Particles

I. 物理環境(A-H)：氣流/HEPA/微粒 | p7-p22

PDA Points to Consider No. 1: Aseptic Processing (Revised 2023) | p7 – p22

本節涵蓋主題 Topics Covered

A.1 氣流速度 A.2 速度量測 A.3 量測頻率 B.1 氣流可視化 B.2 錄影記錄 C 軋蓋環境 D 差壓 E HEPA 測試 F HEPA 修補 G 層流 vs 單向流 H 取樣管路

本章學習目標

  • 理解 Grade A 區域氣流速度建議值（0.45 m/s ±20%）的物理意義與量測位置，以及 EU Annex 1 (2022) 的指引範圍（0.36–0.54 m/s）。
  • 說明氣流可視化（煙霧試驗）的執行時機、動態條件要求、影像記錄義務與保存規範。
  • 掌握差壓梯度（不低於 10 Pa）的目的、連續監測要求、警報策略及氣流反轉的矯正措施。
  • 判斷 HEPA 過濾器的完整性測試頻率（Grade A/B 每 6 個月、Grade C/D 每 12 個月）及修補的法規立場。
  • 區分「層流（laminar flow）」與「單向流（unidirectional airflow）」的術語差異，並連結 EU Annex 1 的對齊立場。
  • 說明顆粒計數取樣管路長度與彎曲半徑的最佳化原則（EU Annex 1 建議 ≤1 m）。
Topic A.1: Airflow Velocity — 氣流速度量測位置

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
Where should airflow velocity measurements be taken with respect to a filling line or other aseptic processing areas?

Recommendation
Airflow velocity measurements should be taken at locations where critical surfaces or products are exposed, and should be protected by "first air," that is, at working height or elsewhere that would yield valuable information (e.g., at a distance of 15–30 cm from filter face). Measurement location may need to be modified due to equipment configuration that results in interference of airflow velocity as identified by risk assessment and rationalized and documented by the contamination control strategy (CCS). Readings should be reproducible.

Rationale
The primary reason for airflow velocity measurements in unidirectional airflow areas (e.g., areas where products, product-contact packaging components, and product-contact surfaces are exposed) is to ensure adequate airflow to protect the materials from external airborne contamination and to verify continued compliance with current smoke studies. The adequacy of the environment can be determined, in part, from airflow velocity and airflow visualization studies, and from particulate matter monitoring (at the working position).

Accurate measurements can be taken and changes over time can be detected when airflow velocities are evaluated at a predetermined distance from the filter surface that is sufficiently close to the filter surface to be reproducible to detect changes in the performance of the filter.

These data must be paired with an airflow visualization study to provide evidence of adequate protection of the aseptic process when the air velocity is in a specific range (and no change in the design of the area has occurred).

The airflow velocity depends on the design of the filling line, room design, and air-handling system. Once velocity is determined, it is important to ensure that the velocity stays within the specified parameters. Routine air velocity measurements should be taken at the same locations used during the initial airflow studies to ensure consistency.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

First Air（第一道空氣）：指直接來自 HEPA 過濾器、尚未經過任何設備或人員的潔淨空氣。暴露中的藥液、容器及產品接觸表面必須始終沐浴在「第一道空氣」之中，確保沒有任何上游污染源的二次風流。

量測位置邏輯：距濾網面 15–30 cm 是「足夠靠近以偵測濾網性能變化、又不受設備干擾」的最佳平衡點。工作高度量測則驗證產品實際暴露位置的保護效果。兩者目的不同，通常需要同時執行。

CCS（Contamination Control Strategy，污染控制策略）：若設備外形干擾氣流，必須在 CCS 中合理化並記錄修改後的量測位置——這是 2022 EU Annex 1 的明確要求。

比喻說明 Analogy

手術室通風標準：想像手術室的無菌罩頂（surgical canopy）從天花板向下吹送過濾後的空氣，確保手術切口上方永遠是「從天花板直達傷口」的乾淨風流，不被手術人員的動作打亂。氣流速度量測就好比護理師定期用風速計確認罩頂風速符合規格——太慢則保護不足，太快則造成渦流反而引入污染。無菌充填（Aseptic Filling）的 Grade A 保護邏輯與此完全相同。

重點提示 Key Notes

速度量測必須與煙霧試驗配對：速度數值本身不能單獨作為「環境足夠保護」的證明。PDA PtC-1 明確指出，必須將速度數據與氣流可視化研究（smoke study）結合，才能提供完整的無菌保護證據。許多公司只有速度記錄而缺乏同期的可視化驗證，這是查廠常見的缺失。

量測位置一致性：例行監測必須使用與初始資格驗證（OQ/PQ）完全相同的量測點，才能偵測出濾網性能的長期退化趨勢。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼 PDA 要求量測位置須距濾網面 15–30 cm，而不是直接在產品暴露的工作高度量測？兩者有何不同用途？
  2. 若充填機設備外形（如注射針頭載台）干擾了 Grade A 罩頂的氣流量測，依據 PtC-1 應如何處理？需要記錄在哪份文件中？
Topic A.2: Airflow Velocity Measurements — 0.45 m/s 是否為強制要求？

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
Is an airflow velocity of 0.45 meters/sec ± 20% a requirement at the working surface in a critical zone?

Recommendation
Airflow patterns should be sufficient to protect exposed products, product-contact packaging components, and product-contact surfaces from the ingress of potential environmental contaminants outside the critical zone. Unidirectional flow is an important factor in providing this protection.

Although a linear air velocity of 0.45 meters/sec ± 20% when measured 15 cm to 30 cm from the filter face is a commonly recommended range to establish unidirectional airflow, this should not be considered a requirement at the working level. The velocity ranges at the working level and at the filter face should be established and justified in the CCS. Performing this test in conjunction with air visualization studies can also demonstrate the maintenance of unidirectionality at the working height, and this should be done at both at-rest and in-operation situations.

Rationale
Airflow velocity and pattern are dependent upon obstacles encountered within the critical zone, including the filling equipment/line, interventions by personnel, and configuration of the barrier that separates the zone from the outer environment. Unidirectional flow is intended to allow the air to flow smoothly past and around these obstacles with minimal turbulence and no induction of potential contamination from outside the zone. The supply air velocity should be correlated to airflow visualization studies and optimized to produce airflow patterns that protect exposed products, product-contact packaging components, and product-contact surfaces from airborne contamination at the working level. This may be lower (or even higher) than the recommended accepted range.

NOTE (EU Annex 1, 2022): "Unidirectional airflow systems should provide a homogeneous air speed in a range of 0.36–0.54 m/s (guidance value) at the working position, unless otherwise scientifically justified in the CCS. Airflow visualization studies should correlate with the air speed measurement." The air velocity range is specifically indicated as a guidance.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

0.45 m/s ±20% 的由來：這個數值源自 1960–70 年代美國航太工業潔淨室規範（美國 Federal Standard 209），後被製藥業沿用。它的意義是「足以維持單向流動性的經驗值」，而非嚴格的物理必要條件。

PDA vs EU Annex 1 立場比較：

  • PDA PtC-1：0.45 m/s ±20%「不應視為工作高度的強制要求」，應由 CCS 建立並論證。
  • EU Annex 1 (2022)：提供 0.36–0.54 m/s 作為指引值（guidance value），並要求與氣流可視化研究相關聯。
  • 共同底線：兩者均強調「目標是保護產品的單向流動性」，而非死守一個數字。

公式與計算 Formula

EU Annex 1 (2022) 指引範圍（工作位置）：
  下限：0.36 m/s（= 0.45 × 0.80）
  建議：0.45 m/s
  上限：0.54 m/s（= 0.45 × 1.20）

PDA 建議（距濾網面 15–30 cm）：
  0.45 m/s ± 20% → 0.36 – 0.54 m/s

注意：工作高度速度通常低於濾網面速度
因為設備障礙物會分散氣流。
CCS 須分別建立兩個位置的驗收標準。

比喻說明 Analogy

馬路限速標誌 vs 實際行車安全：0.45 m/s 就像高速公路的「建議速度 90 km/h」標誌，並非硬性限速。在山路彎道（充填機設備密集的 Grade A 區）可能需要降速（更低氣流速度），在筆直寬敞路段（開放式罩頂）可能需要稍快才能維持穩定的單向流動性。重點不是速度計上的數字，而是「氣流是否真的保護了產品」——這需要煙霧試驗來確認。

重點提示 Key Notes — FDA vs EU 差異

FDA 2004 Aseptic Processing Guidance 仍常被引用 0.45 m/s，但措辭為「推薦」而非「要求」。
EU Annex 1 (2022) 明確標注 0.36–0.54 m/s 為「guidance value」，允許科學論證偏離。
實務上：若您的設施速度在 0.3 m/s 但煙霧試驗顯示完美的單向保護，並有充分的科學論據記錄於 CCS，FDA/EMA 查廠均可接受。關鍵是「論據」與「文件」，而非硬套數字。

實務應用 Practical Application

CDMO 情境：您的客戶要求在標書（RFP）中保證 Grade A 氣流速度為 0.45 m/s ±20%。但您的充填機因設備外形限制，工作高度實際速度為 0.38 m/s，但煙霧試驗顯示完美保護。

建議做法：在 CCS 中記錄工作高度的驗收標準（如 0.35–0.55 m/s），附上煙霧試驗報告作為科學論據，並向客戶解釋 PDA 與 EU Annex 1 均不要求死守 0.45 m/s。這樣既符合法規，也能讓客戶理解。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. EU Annex 1 (2022) 與 PDA PtC-1 在 0.45 m/s 的立場是否一致？各自的措辭關鍵字是什麼？
  2. 若工作高度速度低於 0.36 m/s，但煙霧試驗結果良好，法規上可以接受嗎？需要哪些文件支撐？
Topic A.3: Airflow Velocity Measurement Frequency — 量測頻率

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
When do airflow velocity measurements have to be taken?

Recommendation
Airflow velocity measurements should be taken during operational and performance qualification studies. High-efficiency particulate air (HEPA) filters in critical zones (i.e., Grade A and surrounding Grade B areas) should then be tested every six months, and the frequency of testing HEPA filters in other areas should be at least annually. More frequent measurements may be appropriate if other measures of cleanroom quality indicate a significant deviation (e.g., increased airborne particulates).

The impact of air velocity levels that are outside validated acceptance criteria should be evaluated by performing airflow visualization studies as part of applicable change-management procedures.

Rationale
Airflow velocity is measured to ensure adequate airflow to protect exposed products, product-contact packaging components, and product-contact surfaces. It is also measured to ensure that there have been no significant changes to the performance of the heating, ventilation, and air conditioning (HVAC) system. Airflow criteria are established during qualification studies.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

頻率要求一覽：

  • OQ/PQ 期間：必須執行（建立基準值）
  • Grade A + 周邊 Grade B：每 6 個月（半年一次）
  • 其他區域（Grade C、D）：至少每 12 個月（每年一次）
  • 例外觸發（ad-hoc）：顆粒數異常升高、HVAC 系統重大變更、查廠前

值得注意：「氣流速度量測頻率」與「HEPA 完整性測試頻率」在 PtC-1 中是同步的（見 Topic E），二者通常一起執行。

公式與計算 Formula — 年度測試行事曆

Grade A / Grade B 測試週期：
  1月 → 7月 → 1月 → ...（每6個月）

Grade C / Grade D 測試週期：
  1月 → 1月（每12個月）

若有顆粒數 OOS 事件：
  → 立即執行氣流可視化研究
  → 評估速度是否偏離驗收標準
  → 啟動變更管理程序

比喻說明 Analogy

汽車定期保養：Grade A 每 6 個月測一次氣流速度，就像賽車每場比賽前必須檢查煞車性能，因為風險最高；Grade C/D 就像一般家用車每年一次年度保養。重點是：「風險越高，保養頻率越高」。HVAC 異常就是「行駛中警示燈亮起」，需要立即停下檢查，不能等到下一個排程保養。

重點提示 Key Notes

速度超出驗收標準時的處理邏輯：不能僅記錄偏差並調整設定值就了事。PDA PtC-1 明確要求必須以「氣流可視化研究」評估影響，並作為適用的「變更管理程序（change-management procedures）」的一部分。這意味著速度 OOS 事件必須觸發一次完整的煙霧試驗重新評估。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 如果 Grade A 區域半年度氣流速度量測發現偏低，但環境監測（EM）數據均在標準內，是否需要立即停產調查？
  2. HEPA 過濾器在 10 月完成了 PQ 驗證，下一次半年度測試應安排在何時？
Topic B.1: Airflow Visualization — 氣流可視化研究

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
What is the purpose of airflow visualization studies and how often should they be performed?

Recommendation
Airflow visualization studies should be used to evaluate airflow patterns in critical zones including Grade A and Grade B to ensure there is no ingress at interfaces from the surrounding environment. Such studies are recommended for the qualification of new or renovated facilities or of changes in facilities. In particular, airflow visualization studies should be done during qualification studies, and the studies should be repeated when any significant changes are made that might have an impact on study results (e.g., changes to air-handling systems, aseptic processing equipment, HEPA filters, air return risers/outlets, effectiveness of barrier systems, such as restricted access barrier system (RABS) doors) and after periodic intervals that are consistent with the capabilities and level of process monitoring of the air-handling system.

For Grade A airflow, visualization studies should also be performed to assess if new and current interventions are in compliance with good aseptic working principles. Evaluation of these interventions should show that they are appropriate to meet first-air principles. These interventions should then be simulated and assessed in aseptic process simulation (APS) runs, and finally be included in the list of authorized interventions.

Airflow visualization studies can also be used for investigative purposes (e.g., in cases of contamination) and can be very effective training tools.

Visualized airflow patterns should be executed in operational (dynamic) conditions to understand the impact of moving parts and personnel interventions on the actual airflow. In situ air-pattern analysis should be conducted at the critical zones to demonstrate unidirectional airflow and sweeping action over and away from the product under dynamic conditions.

The decision and frequency of repeated air visualization studies should be based on a risk assessment of the process and capabilities of the air system. Even where no changes are believed to have occurred and where monitoring indicates that the airflow remains in a state of control, it is prudent to consider periodic air visualization studies. Where that period of time exceeds 5 years, additional justification for that length of time may be necessary.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

氣流可視化研究（Airflow Visualization Study / Smoke Study）：使用乾冰煙霧、油質煙霧或液態氮等煙霧介質，在潔淨室動態（in-operation）條件下，拍攝氣流流動型態，確認：

  • 產品暴露區始終在「第一道空氣」保護下
  • 操作人員介入不破壞 Grade A 保護
  • 氣流從較潔淨區域向較不潔淨區域流動（無反轉）
  • RABS 門開關不造成外部污染入侵

觸發時機（必須執行）：新廠建立、重大設備變更、HEPA 更換、RABS/隔離器門設計變更、APS 前評估。

比喻說明 Analogy

游泳池排水試驗：想像在游泳池中滴入彩色染料，觀察水流走向——哪裡形成死角、哪裡水流回流。氣流可視化就是同樣的概念：煙霧是「染料」，HEPA 罩頂是「注水口」，充填機設備是「障礙物」。死角（渦流）等於微生物污染的高風險點，設計師必須重新調整設備布局或氣流方向來消除死角。

重點提示 Key Notes — 超過 5 年未重做需額外論證

PDA PtC-1 明確指出：若距上次氣流可視化研究超過 5 年，需要「額外的時間論證」。這在查廠中是高頻缺失點——許多設施在 PQ 驗證時執行一次煙霧試驗後，即使設備多次小幅調整也未重新執行。

EU Annex 1 (2022) Section 4.15 則要求在較不重要區域也需驗證氣流從潔淨到不潔淨方向的流動，這比舊版要求更嚴格。

實務應用 Practical Application

授權介入清單（Authorized Interventions List）的建立流程：
1. 首先在動態條件下執行煙霧試驗，確認各介入動作（如更換充填針、取樣）不破壞 Grade A 氣流。
2. 將通過的介入動作納入 APS（無菌製程模擬）中驗證，確認實際操作不引入污染。
3. 最後將完成驗證的介入列入「授權介入清單」，每次作業只允許執行清單內的動作。
這是 EU Annex 1 (2022) 對介入管理的完整閉環要求。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼氣流可視化研究必須在「動態（in-operation）」條件下執行？靜態（at-rest）條件的結果有何侷限性？
  2. 某 CDMO 客戶更換了充填機型號，但 Grade A 罩頂 HEPA 系統沒有改變，是否需要重新執行煙霧試驗？依據是什麼？
  3. 煙霧試驗結果顯示某操作員的介入動作造成輕微渦流，但沒有直接打到開口容器，應如何處理？
Topic B.2: Airflow Visualization Recording — 影像記錄要求

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
Should airflow visualization studies be recorded?

Recommendation
Airflow visualization studies should be recorded (typically by video), and the review and approval of the video recording should be documented and retained. Written conclusions should be reported to describe the outcomes of these tests. Preferably, the source of smoke generation should cause minimal contamination of the area. The quantity of smoke generated should be appropriate for the size of the area being evaluated and sufficient to clearly discern the airflow pattern. The impact of operator intervention and equipment operation during aseptic processing should be investigated during airflow visualization studies.

Multiple angles may be needed to provide an accurate representation of airflow.

Video recordings are electronic data and must be retained and maintained accordingly. Records of airflow visualization studies should also be used as training material for personnel operating in cleanrooms.

Rationale
Due to the fact that video recordings provide a two-dimensional visualization, multiple angles may be needed to provide an accurate representation of three-dimensional airflow visualization.

Recordings allow for additional evaluation of the study at any successive time, by employees who did not participate in their execution, and for training purposes.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

影像記錄的法規屬性：PDA PtC-1 明確指出影像（video）屬於「電子數據（electronic data）」，必須依照電子數據管理規範（GDocP/Annex 11/21 CFR Part 11）進行保存。這意味著：

  • 原始影像不得刪除或篡改
  • 需建立審閱與批准的電子簽名記錄
  • 保存期限依批次記錄規範（通常產品上市後至少 1 年或產品有效期 +1 年）
  • 影像必須清晰到可以辨識氣流型態——模糊或低解析度的記錄不可接受

重點提示 Key Notes — 多角度拍攝

三維空間問題：Grade A 罩頂的氣流是三維的（X、Y、Z 軸），但單一攝影機只能捕捉二維平面。若只從正面拍攝，可能遺漏側面渦流；只從上方拍攝，可能看不到底部回流。

實務建議：至少從前方、側面各至少 2 個角度拍攝，關鍵操作動作（如開 RABS 門、換充填針）需要近距離特寫。所有角度的影像均需包含在最終報告中。

比喻說明 Analogy

法庭監視器規範：銀行保險庫的監視錄影有嚴格的保存與防篡改規定，因為它是犯罪調查的關鍵證據。氣流可視化影像的地位完全類似——它是「無菌製程保護有效性」的電子證據。FDA 或 EMA 查廠人員有權要求調閱原始影像，確認與報告結論一致。若影像遺失或品質不佳，等同於「監視器壞掉了」，是嚴重的 GMP 缺失。

實務應用 Practical Application

煙霧試驗的清潔程序：PtC-1 提醒使用的煙霧介質應「盡量少污染潔淨室」。實務上，油質煙霧會殘留在 HEPA 濾網和設備表面，試驗後需要依照已驗證的清潔 SOP（包含表面清潔、EM 採樣確認）恢復到潔淨室規格。這個清潔驗證本身也需要記錄並列入試驗方案。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 氣流可視化影像為何被歸類為「電子數據」？這對影像的管理方式有何具體影響？
  2. 您在進行煙霧試驗時，影像顯示某角度有輕微渦流，但另一角度正常。是否可以只提交正常角度的影像？理由為何？
Topic C: Grade A Environment Over Cappers — 軋蓋區域的環境要求

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
What are the recommended environmental conditions for capping aseptically processed, stoppered vials when the capping takes place outside of a Grade A environment?

Recommendation
When capping is undertaken as a clean process outside a Grade A environment, a Grade A air supply over the capping machine is sufficient, provided validated automatic checks for all the vials (e.g., using a missing/raised stopper detector) are in place immediately prior to, or in front of, the capping station to reject any vials with stoppers that do not remain properly seated before they enter the capping and sealing station. The HEPA filters used should be requalified periodically as described in Section I, Topic E.

Monitoring requirements for total particulate and microbiological contamination at the capping machine outside the aseptic core should be defined by the company following a risk assessment.

NOTE (EU Annex 1): When vial capping is undertaken as a clean process outside the aseptic core, stoppered vials should be protected with a Grade A air supply until the cap has been crimped. It also states that RABS and isolators may be beneficial in assuring the required conditions.

Rationale
A properly seated stopper represents an adequately sealed container and a microbiological barrier. Therefore, efforts should be taken to ensure that the container is maintained under conditions that will not add contamination until it is properly stoppered prior to capping. When there is a risk that the stopper might be raised prior to capping, steps should be taken to reject those vials.

A qualified aseptic filling process includes assurance of the proper routine placement of stoppers, as aligned with container closure integrity requirements. A missing or raised stopper-detector must be qualified and challenged on a routine basis and units with compromised or non-integral stoppers should be rejected before capping.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

軋蓋（Capping/Crimping）的位置選擇：軋蓋在工業上通常有兩種配置：

  • 配置 1：在 Grade A 區域內軋蓋（最高保護）
  • 配置 2：在 Grade A 氣流供應下、但位於 Grade A 區域外（本 Topic 討論的情境）

配置 2 的核心前提是：「正確就座的瓶塞本身即是微生物屏障」。因此，只要確保瓶塞完整（透過自動檢測剔除），在乾淨的 Grade A 氣流供應下軋蓋即可接受。

關鍵控制點：軋蓋前必須有已驗證的自動化瓶塞偵測系統（missing/raised stopper detector），且需定期挑戰（challenge testing）。

重點提示 Key Notes — PDA vs EU Annex 1 差異

PDA PtC-1：軋蓋機上方有 Grade A 氣流供應即足夠，監測要求由公司依風險評估定義。
EU Annex 1 (2022)：要求在整個軋蓋完成前，瓶子必須持續受到 Grade A 氣流供應的保護（not just at the machine, but until the cap has been crimped），並建議考慮 RABS 或隔離器（Isolator）以確保條件。
結論：EU 標準比 PDA 要求更嚴格，CDMO 若以歐洲市場為目標，應遵循 EU Annex 1 的解讀。

比喻說明 Analogy

快遞包裝密封檢查：想像一件精密儀器，在包裝車間（相當於無菌充填區）放入泡棉保護後，送到另一個房間（相當於軋蓋區）進行外盒封裝。如果外盒封裝前確認泡棉沒有脫落（相當於瓶塞自動偵測），並在乾淨的環境下完成封裝，整體保護效果是可接受的。但如果泡棉可能鬆動，就必須在與包裝車間相同等級的環境中完成封裝（在 Grade A 區內軋蓋）。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 一家 CDMO 的軋蓋站位於 Grade B 區域，上方有 Grade A 層流罩，且有自動化瓶塞偵測系統。依據 PDA PtC-1 和 EU Annex 1，這樣的配置是否合規？有何差異？
  2. 瓶塞偵測系統需要多久挑戰一次？挑戰方式為何？若挑戰失敗，已生產的批次如何處理？
Topic D: Differential Pressure — 差壓管理

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
What should be the air-pressure differential between zones of differing cleanliness classification (e.g., between Grade B and Grade C zones)?

Recommendation
Positive pressure between zones with different air cleanliness classifications should ensure airflow direction from the "cleaner" toward the "less clean" zones.

A prolonged zero-pressure differential between such zones, or a pressure reversal to the extent that the cleanliness of the environment is compromised, must be avoided.

A pressure differential between different classified zones of not less than 10 pascals (with doors closed) is commonly expected. However, because the principal purpose is to ensure that a minimum measurable positive pressure is maintained, other differential pressure levels may be required based on facility complexity, HVAC system design, and operational characteristics.

An appropriate pressure differential is principally maintained by interlocked and alarmed air locks and doors between the zones of different cleanliness levels and should be continuously monitored by differential pressure devices. Although brief periods of low- or zero-differential pressure may exist between an area and an air lock (of the same grade) with a door open, a measurable pressure differential should be maintained between areas (of different grades) separated by the air lock.

An alarm strategy with appropriately qualified alarm delay limits should be defined for changes to differential pressure and/or pressure drops and should be underpinned by quality risk management. Transient low- or zero-differential pressure occurrences represent critical alarm functions, and these alarms must indicate airflow inversions that are assessed to pose a risk to cleanliness of the area.

Inversion of airflow may be rectified by such steps as:

  • Room balancing (e.g., volume of air and differential pressure adjustments in adjacent rooms) and air-exchange rate of the room
  • Changes in sequence and/or timing of door openings
  • Process and cleanroom design (use of interlocks)
  • Clearing obstructions from air returns

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

差壓（Differential Pressure, dP）的物理目的：確保空氣永遠從「較潔淨（更高等級）」的區域流向「較不潔淨（較低等級）」的區域，阻止微生物、顆粒從外部環境侵入潔淨核心。

基本要求：

  • 最低差壓：10 Pa（關門狀態）——這是業界通行的期望值
  • 必須連續監測（非間歇式）
  • 必須有警報系統（帶有適當的延遲設定，避免開門時的短暫低壓觸發誤報）
  • 警報策略必須有 QRM（品質風險管理）支撐

注意：10 Pa 是「通常期望值（commonly expected）」，非硬性法規數值。設施可依複雜度設定不同值，但必須有論據。

比喻說明 Analogy

差壓如同水壩：想像一個水壩系統——Grade A 是最高水位水庫，Grade B 次之，Grade C、D 依序遞減。水（相當於空氣）永遠從高處流向低處，不會逆流。差壓就是這個「高度落差」的量度。若某段水位差歸零（差壓為零），代表兩個水庫水位相同，一旦有擾動（開門、設備震動），就可能發生雙向流動（逆流），骯髒的水就會流入潔淨的水庫。10 Pa 的差壓就是確保有「足夠高度落差」的最低安全閾值。

公式與計算 Formula — 典型差壓梯度設計

典型梯度設計（由內而外）：
  Grade A（核心）：最高壓力（如 +60 Pa 相對大氣）
  Grade B          ：次高（如 +50 Pa）  ΔP = 10 Pa
  Grade C          ：中等（如 +40 Pa）  ΔP = 10 Pa
  Grade D          ：較低（如 +30 Pa）  ΔP = 10 Pa
  一般環境          ：大氣壓（0 Pa 基準）

注意：含致敏性或高毒性物質的設施
可能需要負壓（negative pressure）
以防物質外洩，此時梯度設計相反。

重點提示 Key Notes — 警報策略設計

延遲警報（Alarm Delay）的必要性：門開啟時差壓必然短暫下降，若沒有適當的延遲設定（如 5–30 秒），HVAC 系統的警報將不斷誤觸發，增加操作員的「警報疲勞（alarm fatigue）」，反而掩蓋了真正的危險信號。

EU Annex 1 (2022) 要求差壓系統必須記錄並報告，且異常必須被評估。美國 FDA 對持續低差壓事件通常會追問根本原因及批次影響評估。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 生產過程中差壓警報觸發，顯示 Grade B 相對 Grade C 差壓降至 5 Pa 持續 2 分鐘，但門並未開啟。應啟動哪些調查步驟？是否影響此期間生產的批次？
  2. 為什麼含有高毒性 API 的設施可能需要「負壓」而非「正壓」設計？差壓梯度如何設計？
  3. 差壓警報延遲時間（alarm delay）應如何確定？依據是什麼？
Topic E: Testing of HEPA Filters — HEPA 過濾器測試

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
What is the frequency with which HEPA filters should be tested?

Recommendation
HEPA-filter testing should comprise integrity testing, airflow volume measurement, and airflow velocity testing. HEPA filters should be tested minimally upon initial installation and replacement. Requalification frequency should be based on a risk assessment using historical performance, available data, cleanroom design, and usage.

HEPA-filter performance characteristics for Grade A (and surrounding Grade B) areas should be requalified at a maximum interval of six months. For lower-grade areas (Grades C, Grade D, and remaining Grade B areas not required to be supplied with unidirectional airflow), a maximum interval of 12 months applies. The airflow velocity testing may be replaced with recovery testing. The frequency of recovery testing in these lower grade areas should be determined based on risk assessment.

In lower-grade areas where airflow is unidirectional the air velocity testing should be based on risk assessment.

Production campaigns should be scheduled to allow for requalification. Where exceptions occur that result in a delay in a periodic requalification, the requalification should be performed as soon as possible after the delay and the risk of such a delay on product quality should be evaluated.

Where testing indicates a HEPA filter integrity or performance failure, steps should be taken to repair or replace the filter, or otherwise address the failure, and steps should also be taken to address product impact from the failure.

Rationale
Because routine monitoring is not sensitive enough to assure the performance of the HEPA filter system or individual HEPA filters, periodic retesting of the HEPA-filter system and individual HEPAs is beneficial, as reflected in EU Annex 1 and other health authority guidances.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

HEPA（High-Efficiency Particulate Air）過濾器測試的三要素：

  • 完整性測試（Integrity Test）：即 DOP/PAO 測試（Dispersed Oil Particulate / Poly-alpha Olefin），以氣溶膠挑戰 HEPA 濾網，確認無針孔或密封缺陷。測試儀器需定期校正。
  • 氣流量測（Airflow Volume Measurement）：確認通過濾網的總風量符合設計規格。
  • 氣流速度測試（Airflow Velocity Testing）：與 Topic A.3 的要求一致（Grade A/B 每 6 個月）。

恢復測試（Recovery Testing）：在低等級區域（Grade C/D），可以用「潔淨室恢復時間測試」替代氣流速度測試，量測潔淨室在人工污染後恢復到規格內顆粒數的時間，間接確認 HVAC 系統效能。

公式與計算 Formula — 測試頻率矩陣

┌─────────────┬──────────────┬──────────────┐
│ 區域分級     │ 最大測試間隔  │ 觸發條件      │
├─────────────┼──────────────┼──────────────┤
│ Grade A      │ 6 個月       │ 安裝、更換、  │
│ Grade B      │ 6 個月       │ 顆粒數 OOS、  │
│ (UDAF 供應) │              │ HVAC 異常     │
├─────────────┼──────────────┼──────────────┤
│ Grade C      │ 12 個月      │ 安裝、更換、  │
│ Grade D      │ 12 個月      │ 重大變更      │
│ Grade B      │ 12 個月      │               │
│ (非 UDAF)  │              │               │
└─────────────┴──────────────┴──────────────┘

失效時處理：
  修補（見 Topic F）或更換 → 完整性 + 速度重測
  → 評估產品影響 → 批次處置決策

重點提示 Key Notes

排程延誤的處理：PtC-1 提醒，若因生產排程延誤了例行資格重驗（requalification），應盡快補測，並評估延誤期間對產品品質的風險。這是一個重要的 CAPA 觸發點——不能僅以「生產繁忙」作為理由而無正式評估記錄。

HEPA 失效的批次評估：若測試發現 HEPA 有針孔或完整性失效，必須回溯評估哪些批次可能受到影響（worst-case 方向：從上次通過測試之後生產的所有批次）。這可能導致批次保留或拒絕放行。

實務應用 Practical Application

CDMO 資格維護行事曆設計：建議將 HEPA 測試與氣流速度量測整合進同一次「半年度設施再資格驗證（semi-annual facility requalification）」，與 APS（無菌製程模擬）的排程協調，避免出現連續停產。一般而言，設施再資格占滿 3–5 個工作日（視設施規模），應提前 2–3 個月向客戶告知停產計畫。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. HEPA 完整性測試（PAO test）的原理是什麼？「通過」的判斷標準（acceptance criteria）通常是什麼？
  2. 若 Grade A HEPA 在 6 個月測試時發現一個小針孔（pinhole），但環境監測數據在整個期間均正常，是否需要拒絕放行所有在此期間生產的批次？如何評估？
Topic F: HEPA Filter Patching — HEPA 過濾器修補

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
Can HEPA filters be patched? If so, what is the maximum allowable patch size?

Recommendation
HEPA-filter patching for Grade A should be avoided. HEPA-filter patching for Grade B–D should proceed only after the repair is justified by careful risk assessment, the repair is performed to industry standards to ensure patch durability, and aseptic process production should only commence after the performance of the repaired HEPA-filter has been verified to show that it has returned to a qualified state. Testing should include leak and velocity testing. If the testing does not verify that the repaired HEPA has returned to a qualified state, then the HEPA should be repaired if possible or replaced.

HEPA filters can be repaired or patched, but the company should develop a rationale for allowable filter repair shape and size fit for the different installation and area classifications based on a thorough risk assessment.

If this rationale supports repair, HEPA filters may be patched with room-temperature vulcanization silicone or other suitable material as long as filter integrity is restored and the airflow volume and velocity through the filter are not significantly affected (i.e., room pressure differentials and airflow patterns remain as validated).

Industry standards for patch size:

  • IEST-RP-CC001.5: Not to exceed an area of 13 cm² (2 in²) in any one patch, or a total of 1% of the area being patched.
  • EN ISO 29463-4: All repairs together shall not block or restrict more than 0.5% of the filter face area and the maximum length of each single repair shall not exceed 3.0 cm.
  • IEST RP-CC034.5: Field repair should not block or restrict more than an additional 3.0% of the filter face area, and no single repair should have a lesser dimension exceeding 3.8 cm (1.5 in.).
  • ISO 14644-3, Section B.6.6: Allows for repairs "by agreement between the customer and supplier."
NOTE (EU Annex 1): Requires precautions when carrying out this type of intervention, such as restricting access to the work area, clearly defining work protocols, and cleaning, disinfecting, and environmental monitoring being considered.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Grade A 的立場：不建議修補（avoid）
Grade A 是最高風險區域，其 HEPA 過濾器任何修補的結果均難以與新濾網的完整性相比擬。PDA 的立場是「避免（avoid）」，而不是「禁止（prohibit）」——雖然有此區別，但實務上查廠人員對 Grade A 修補持極嚴格態度。

Grade B–D 的立場：可修補，但有條件
必須要有：(1) 風險評估論據、(2) 行業標準支撐的修補規格、(3) 修補後的完整性與速度再測試通過。不同標準（IEST、ISO、EN ISO）對「最大修補面積」的規定略有差異，公司需選定一個並記錄在 SOP 中。

比喻說明 Analogy

安全帽破損是否繼續戴：假設你的安全帽（相當於 HEPA 過濾器）在意外中出現小裂縫，你有幾個選擇：(A) 直接扔掉換新的（Grade A 建議做法）；(B) 用特殊膠帶補好，然後請專業機構重新測試強度（Grade B–D 修補流程）；(C) 不管裂縫繼續戴（絕對不可接受）。關鍵在於：你用來騎摩托車（Grade B）還是賽車頭盔（Grade A）——後者的標準更高，裂縫寧可換新，不冒任何風險。

重點提示 Key Notes — 不同標準的修補規格差異

標準 單一修補最大面積 總修補面積上限 最大長度
IEST-RP-CC001.5 13 cm² 1% of filter face —
EN ISO 29463-4 — 0.5% of filter face 3.0 cm
IEST RP-CC034.5 — 3.0% additional 3.8 cm (1.5 in)
ISO 14644-3 B.6.6 依客戶與供應商協議

EU Annex 1 額外要求修補作業必須有隔離管制（限制人員進入）、明確的作業規程，以及事後的清潔、消毒和環境監測。這些步驟必須記錄在書面程序中。

實務應用 Practical Application

修補 SOP 建立要點（Grade B–D）：
1. 風險評估：評估破損位置（中央 vs 邊緣）、大小、可能受影響的製程。
2. 修補規格：選定適用的行業標準（通常採 EN ISO 29463-4 因歐洲市場），明確最大修補面積與長度。
3. 修補材料：記錄使用的材料（如室溫硫化矽膠，RTV silicone）及批號。
4. 修補後測試：完整性測試（PAO）+ 速度測試，兩者均需通過才可恢復生產。
5. EU Annex 1 要求：修補作業區隔離 + 事後清潔消毒 + EM 採樣。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. Grade A 的 HEPA 如果需要修補，PDA 的立場是「避免」而非「禁止」，在什麼極端情況下可能考慮修補而非直接更換？需要哪些額外條件？
  2. EN ISO 29463-4 和 IEST-RP-CC001.5 對修補面積的規定不同，公司應如何選擇適用的標準？選定後需要做什麼？
Topic G: Laminar vs Unidirectional Airflow — 術語澄清

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
Should airflow in Grade A critical zones be laminar or unidirectional?

Recommendation
Airflow in critical Grade A zones (i.e., where products or sterile components are exposed) should be unidirectional. In aseptic processing, unidirectional airflow means that the air mass flows from the source (i.e., the HEPA filter) in one direction into or over the critical zone and its contents in such a way as to ensure that the exposed products and sterile components are always in air that has not passed any other component, operator, or equipment that has not been sterilized. This is the concept of first air.

"NOTE: In closed isolators, turbulent flow may be acceptable for Grade A zones when it is supported by operational qualification demonstrating the maintenance of acceptable particulate levels."

Rationale
The term "laminar," although used historically in this context, is problematic. True laminar airflow is virtually impossible to achieve in physical environments. Moreover, true laminar airflow is not necessary to achieve appropriate airflow that maintains the first-air concept.

ISO 14644-3:2019 defines unidirectional airflow as "controlled airflow through the entire cross-section of a clean zone with a steady velocity and approximately parallel streamlines."

The first-air approach applies to all airflow situations and aseptic processing methods where contamination through airborne means might be a risk.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

術語演變的歷史背景：

  • Laminar Flow（層流）：物理學術語，指雷諾數（Reynolds number）極低時流體中每個粒子完全平行流動，不發生任何混合。在真實潔淨室環境中（有設備、人員、溫度差），這幾乎不可能實現。
  • Unidirectional Airflow（單向流）：業界改用的實用術語（ISO 14644-3 定義），重點在「穩定速度」和「大致平行的流線」，允許小程度的渦流，但總體方向一致。

EU Annex 1 (2022) 的對齊：EU Annex 1 全文改用「unidirectional airflow（單向氣流）」取代舊版的「laminar flow（層流）」，與 ISO 14644 和本 PDA PtC-1 的建議完全對齊。

比喻說明 Analogy

河流 vs 水道：「層流」就像理想狀態下靜止水槽中的完全平行流動，現實中幾乎不存在。「單向流」就像設計良好的人工水道——雖然水流過障礙物時會有小渦流，但整體上從上游流向下游，不會倒流。充填線 Grade A 區域就是這樣的「人工水道」：設備是障礙物，但只要主體氣流方向是從 HEPA 向下（或向前），就達到了保護產品的目的。

重點提示 Key Notes — 隔離器的例外

PDA PtC-1 提出一個重要例外：密閉隔離器（Closed Isolators）中，湍流（turbulent flow）在 Grade A 區域可以被接受——前提是 OQ 必須證明能維持可接受的顆粒水平。

這個例外的邏輯是：密閉隔離器本身提供了極高的物理屏障保護，即使氣流非單向，外部污染也無法進入。因此，保護機制是「密封屏障」而非「氣流方向」。這與開放式或半開放式 RABS 系統完全不同。

實務應用 Practical Application

文件中的術語一致性：許多舊版 SOP、驗證方案和批次記錄仍使用「laminar flow」。建議在下一次文件審閱周期中統一更換為「unidirectional airflow（單向氣流）」，以與 EU Annex 1 (2022)、ISO 14644 及 PDA PtC-1 保持一致，避免查廠時引發監管質疑。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼「真正的層流（true laminar flow）」在製藥潔淨室中幾乎不可能實現？哪些物理因素使其難以達成？
  2. 密閉隔離器（Closed Isolator）中允許湍流的理由是什麼？這與開放式 RABS 系統有何根本差異？
  3. 如果公司的 URS（用戶需求規格）中要求「laminar flow for Grade A」，是否需要更新？為什麼？
Topic H: Length and Radii of Airborne Sampling Tubing — 取樣管路設計

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement
How should tubing for total particulate sampling be configured?

Recommendation
The sample tubing length and number of bends should be minimized. Bend radii should be maximized in accordance with the recommended practices from the equipment manufacturer and should be technically justified. Tubing with bends should be sized so that the bend radii do not change.

Rationale
Each unique particle size will have a different deposition profile in tubing based on, for example, airflow velocity and sample volume, tubing diameter, sampling port arrangement, temperature, bend radius, tube length, and tubing material. Because it is a range of sizes (e.g., 0.5 microns and greater in optical diameter) that particulate monitoring attempts to assess, no single set of radii or length conditions can describe best practices for each of these particle sizes. Minimizing the number of tubing bends, maximizing radii, and minimizing overall tubing length should be the goal and should be done in accordance with the particle-counter equipment manufacturer's recommended best practices.

The particle-counter equipment manufacturer should provide a technical justification for its recommendations. Instrument calibration should address sampling configuration.

NOTE (EU Annex 1, 2022): Tube length should typically be no longer than 1 m.
NOTE (ISO 14644-1:2015): Tube length should be no longer than 1 m.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

為什麼管路長度和彎曲半徑很重要？

顆粒計數器是通過管路將潔淨室中的空氣樣品吸引到感測器。管路過長或彎曲過多，會造成顆粒在管壁上的靜電沉積（electrostatic deposition）或慣性損失（inertial loss），使到達感測器的顆粒數少於實際環境中的顆粒數，導致監測數據失真（低估污染）。

關鍵設計原則：

  • 管路長度：盡量短，EU Annex 1 和 ISO 14644-1 均建議不超過 1 m
  • 彎曲次數：盡量少（每個彎曲都造成顆粒損失）
  • 彎曲半徑：盡量大（半徑越小，慣性衝擊越嚴重）
  • 等速取樣（Isokinetic sampling）：取樣入口速度應與環境氣流速度匹配，避免過採或漏採

公式與計算 Formula — 顆粒損失機制

主要顆粒損失機制：
1. 慣性撞擊（Inertial Impaction）
   → 顆粒在彎曲處無法跟隨氣流轉向
   → 解決：最大化彎曲半徑 R/D ≥ 5

2. 重力沉降（Gravitational Settling）
   → 大顆粒（>5 μm）在水平管段沉降
   → 解決：最小化水平管路長度

3. 靜電沉積（Electrostatic Deposition）
   → 帶電顆粒吸附管壁
   → 解決：使用靜電消散材料（ESD tubing）

EU Annex 1 / ISO 14644-1 要求：
   管路總長度 ≤ 1 m

比喻說明 Analogy

吸管喝珍珠奶茶：想像用一根很長、彎曲很多的細吸管喝珍珠奶茶——很多珍珠（相當於顆粒）會被卡在彎曲處或沉在管底，真正吸到嘴裡的比杯子裡的少很多。顆粒計數器的取樣管路面臨完全一樣的問題。如果吸管短而直（管路短、少彎曲），幾乎每個珍珠都能順利通過；如果吸管長且彎曲複雜，監測結果就會嚴重低估環境中的實際顆粒數。

重點提示 Key Notes — PDA vs EU Annex 1 差異

PDA PtC-1：管路長度和彎曲應「最小化」，但沒有規定具體的長度數值——強調依據廠商建議和技術論證。
EU Annex 1 (2022) 和 ISO 14644-1：明確建議管路長度「通常不超過 1 m」。
實務影響：若 Grade A 遠端監測（如 RABS 內部取樣點）因設備配置必須使用較長管路，必須有技術論證（例如：廠商提供的顆粒回收率 (particle recovery efficiency) 測試報告），並在 CCS 中記錄。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. EU Annex 1 建議取樣管路不超過 1 m，但您的 RABS 設計中，取樣頭距儀器主機需要 1.5 m 的管路。應如何論證這個偏離是可接受的？
  2. 取樣管路的「等速取樣（isokinetic sampling）」是什麼意思？為什麼取樣入口速度需要與環境氣流速度匹配？
  3. 顆粒計數器的儀器校正（instrument calibration）中，PDA PtC-1 提到應「address sampling configuration（涵蓋取樣配置）」，這具體意味著什麼？

本節重點回顧 Section Summary — Topics A–H

  • A.1 量測位置：氣流速度量測應在產品暴露的關鍵表面附近進行，距濾網面 15–30 cm 或工作高度，並需與煙霧試驗數據配對使用。量測位置的任何修改均需在 CCS 中論證。
  • A.2 速度數值：0.45 m/s ±20%（PDA）或 0.36–0.54 m/s（EU Annex 1 指引值）均為「建議範圍」而非硬性要求。目標是在科學論據支撐下，達到保護產品的單向流動性。
  • A.3 量測頻率：Grade A/B 每 6 個月，其他區域至少每年一次；出現顆粒數異常或 HVAC 系統變更時需追加量測。
  • B.1 煙霧試驗：必須在動態（in-operation）條件下執行，驗證操作介入與設備運作對氣流的影響；超過 5 年未重做需提供額外論證；結果應連結 APS 設計和 EM 計畫。
  • B.2 影像記錄：影像屬電子數據，須依 GDocP 保存；需多角度拍攝以完整呈現三維氣流；可作為人員訓練素材。
  • C 軋蓋環境：Grade A 氣流供應 + 已驗證的自動瓶塞偵測系統 = 可接受的配置（PDA）。EU Annex 1 更進一步要求在整個軋蓋完成前持續提供 Grade A 保護。
  • D 差壓：不同等級間需維持 ≥10 Pa（通行期望值），需連續監測並設置帶 QRM 支撐的警報策略；差壓反轉必須即時調查並評估產品影響。
  • E HEPA 測試：Grade A/B 每 6 個月、Grade C/D 每 12 個月完整性+速度測試；失效必須評估批次影響並啟動修補或更換程序。
  • F HEPA 修補：Grade A 避免修補（首選更換）；Grade B–D 可修補，但需風險評估 + 符合業界標準規格 + 修補後再測試通過。EU Annex 1 要求修補作業有隔離管制與事後環境監測。
  • G 術語：應使用「單向流（unidirectional airflow）」而非「層流（laminar flow）」，與 EU Annex 1 (2022) 和 ISO 14644 對齊。密閉隔離器中湍流可被接受（需 OQ 支撐）。
  • H 取樣管路：管路長度最小化（EU Annex 1 / ISO 14644-1 建議 ≤1 m）、彎曲最少且半徑最大化；偏離需技術論證，並在儀器校正中涵蓋取樣配置。
1b

Topic 1b: I. Physical Environment (I-O): RABS, Isolators, BFS, Airlocks

I. 物理環境(I-O)：RABS/隔離器/BFS/氣鎖 | p23-p36

主題 I–O：物理環境 — RABS、吹-填-封、氣閘與粒子監測
PDA Points to Consider No. 1 (2023) | p23 – p36 PtC-1

本章學習目標 Learning Objectives

  • 理解 Isolator（隔離器）、Closed RABS（封閉型限制進出屏障系統）、Open RABS 三者在無菌保護等級上的差異，以及各自適用的環境分級要求。
  • 掌握 Blow-Fill-Seal（BFS，吹瓶-充填-封口）製程的環境控制邏輯：為何 BFS 不需 Grade B 過渡區，其「Grade A 等效」如何透過設計實現。
  • 了解潔淨室「清除期（Clean-Up Period）」的確立方式，以及 EU Annex 1 的 20 分鐘指導值背後的意義。
  • 區別「靜止狀態（At-Rest）」與「操作狀態（In-Operation）」的定義、監測要求，以及 ≥5 µm 粒子監測的限值爭議與實務應對。
  • 掌握氣閘（Air Lock）設計原則：壓力梯度設計、人員通道與物料通道分離，以及 ISO 14644-1 分級採樣量的標準。

本節涵蓋主題 Topics Covered

Topic I: RABS & Isolators Topic J: Clean-Up Period Topic K.1: BFS Process Design Topic K.2: Resin Storage Topic K.3: BFS APS Topic L: Air Locks Topic M: At-Rest vs In-Operation Topic N: Sample Volume Topic O: ≥0.5 & ≥5 µm Monitoring
Topic I: RABS and Isolators — Aseptic Processing Technologies (p23–p26)

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement

What "barrier" systems and practices should be used to reduce the risk of microbiological contamination from human intervention and external environment in aseptic processing systems?

Recommendation

Barrier systems should be used for aseptic processes. Barrier methods typically include isolators and RABS but may also include other technologies where physical separation is achieved. The systems and controls associated with the design and use of barrier systems should be included in the CCS.

Barrier systems are defined as "closed" or "open", based on exposure to the surrounding environment. While all isolators and RABS provide a barrier from personnel and the external environment, closed isolators provide a higher level of protection with respect to open isolator systems and RABS, which require additional precautions and controls to prevent contamination.

Isolators differ from RABS because they usually have automated decontamination systems, employ continuous HEPA-filtered air differential/over-pressure control, are physically sealed from the external environment or, in the case of open isolators, have positive airflow at the product exit and have doors or panels that cannot be opened for any reason during the aseptic process without repeating the decontamination process. As such, isolators should provide a higher level of protection compared to RABS which, in turn, provides a higher level of protection compared to classical curtained manual aseptic processing.

Design and Operation

Isolators and RABS should be designed and operated in such a way as to reduce the risk of microbiological contamination to critical operations, including transfer of materials and components, EM, setup of filling systems, removal of fallen containers or components, fill checks, or other interventions within these systems.

The following should be considered for the design and operation of isolators and RABS:

  • Open isolators may be placed in Grade C environments. Closed isolators may be placed in Grade D environments. RABS should be placed in Grade B environments only. The decontamination and transfer of materials into and out of the isolator and RABS should be qualified, controlled, and monitored to prevent contamination of materials and sterile product.
  • The design should facilitate uncomplicated aseptic setup of the filling line and should negate the need for any contact to critical surfaces (e.g., filling needles) via operator gloves or RABS/isolator gloves and should provide for first-air principles to be maintained within the critical zone.
  • Direct contact of critical surfaces by RABS/isolator gloves should be avoided.
  • The location of glove ports and gloves in isolators and RABS should be designed to facilitate effective and easy performance of interventions by all personnel. Their location and design should provide for first-air protection in the critical zone and should not present an ergonomic challenge to operators that may otherwise result in suboptimal, or a lapse in, aseptic technique during operations.
  • Glove ports, gloves, and transfer ports should remain integral after decontamination and throughout the operation and should be tested regularly for leaks.
  • Gloves should be designed and positioned to avoid damage.
  • The interior of the isolator and RABS, including the positioning of glove ports, gloves, and other equipment, should be designed to facilitate effective decontamination and transfer/movement of materials and product.
  • Isolator and RABS decontamination methods should be validated and controlled to render surfaces and items incapable of contaminating the environment or sterile product.
  • Controls should be in place to maintain a decontaminated state of interior, environment, and materials.
  • The decontamination method should not chemically contaminate or otherwise compromise materials.
  • Equipment and isolator and RABS should be designed to work with operational procedures and aseptic techniques to minimize the need for interventions.

Intervention Control

Proper aseptic techniques should be used to perform activities and interventions in the RABS/isolator. Interventions performed in isolators and RABS should be assessed for risk of contamination to product and should not be permitted if they present an unacceptable increased risk to the aseptic process.

RABS should be designed and operated with doors and panels closed during aseptic processing. Interventions with open doors or panels should be avoided. Where possible, interventions performed in RABS should be performed with doors closed using fixed mounted gloves. Where not possible, interventions performed with open RABS doors should be limited and special controls and precautions should be used.

When processes require open-door interventions, those activities should be assessed for contamination risk, must be part of the qualified list of interventions, and must incorporate additional control measures. Such additional control measures may include:

  • Additional disinfection and sanitization of non-product-contact surfaces using a qualified disinfection agent and procedures, including the interior of doors and panels opened during the activity
  • Door access with recorded intervention alarms or an effective means of documentation
  • Documented line clearance
  • Positive airflow from the enclosure to the surrounding environment when the door is opened, which has been assessed and documented in smoke studies
  • Additional monitoring of product-contact surfaces and interior environment in proximity to activity
  • Additional removal or testing of materials or products exposed to the intervention
  • Monitoring of operator gloves and sleeves immediately after the open-door intervention
  • Air visualization studies or other means to assure that the activity and intervention design allows for performance without disrupting first-air principles

Decontamination

Direct product-contact surfaces, including product and holding vessels, should be sterilized using validated methods and maintained in a sterile state throughout production. Indirect product-contact surfaces (e.g., stopper bowls and tracks) must be rendered free of microbiological contamination. Where possible, sterilization should be used; where not feasible, a validated decontamination method rendering surfaces incapable of contaminating sterile product must be employed.

All interior non-product-contact surfaces, including glove ports, gloves, equipment, transfer ports, container transfer systems, and equipment surfaces should be decontaminated using validated methods. Glove integrity should be monitored frequently, normally at the end of production and after the performance of interventions or activities that may pose a risk to glove integrity.

Failure Investigation

Personnel can still be the source of contamination in isolators and RABS if the process or equipment design is flawed or if activities are not performed properly. Special consideration should also be given to system and process design, cleaning and disinfection procedures, decontamination process, and proper transfer procedures and material integrity, when investigating critical-zone EM excursions, sterility-test failures, and APS failures.

Rationale

Personnel are a significant source of microbiological contamination. Barrier systems such as isolators and RABS provide physical separation between personnel, external environment, and exposed product or product-contact surfaces. For this reason, they provide more preventive controls and protection than conventional aseptic processing lines located in cleanrooms.

The interior of these systems, including fixed gloves, are decontaminated, and not necessarily sterilized. Therefore, there is a need for proper equipment design, qualified cleaning procedures and use of aseptic technique and first-air principles, and the avoidance of contact with critical surfaces when performing activities and interventions.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — 屏障系統三層次

PDA PtC-1 將無菌製程的屏障防護分為三個等級，保護強度由低到高：

  • 傳統帷幕式手工無菌充填（Classical Curtained Manual）：人員直接在潔淨室操作，依賴 Grade A 層流保護。保護強度最低。
  • RABS（限制進出屏障系統）：透過固定式手套連接的物理圍欄，將操作員手臂與產品空間隔離。需要放置於 Grade B 環境中（自身提供 Grade A 保護）。
  • Isolator（隔離器）：完全密封的氣密空間，配備自動化去污系統（通常為 VHP，氣化過氧化氫）。Open Isolator 需 Grade C；Closed Isolator 僅需 Grade D。保護強度最高。

關鍵：等級越高，對周圍環境分級的要求反而越低，因為設備本身已提供極高的保護。

比喻說明 — 太空站 vs 無塵室

把這三種系統想像成不同等級的「防護空間」：

  • Isolator = 太空站：完全密封於外界環境，太空人（操作員）完全在外面，透過機械臂（手套）操作。太空站（Grade D）周圍即使是真空宇宙（惡劣環境）也無所謂，因為內部完全隔絕。進行任何維修（等同開門干預）都必須先做「艙外行走準備」（重新去污）。
  • RABS = 有圍欄的無塵室：潔淨室（Grade B）中加裝了玻璃圍欄，操作員仍在同一空間裡，只是手伸進去操作。環境的等級還是很重要。
  • 傳統手工充填 = 開放手術室：完全依賴空間潔淨度和操作員技術。

這個比喻也解釋了為何 Isolator 去污後不能隨便開門——就像太空艙開艙門前必須先重新加壓一樣。

重點提示 — 環境分級要求對照

這是監管機構和廠房設計師最常查核的細節：

技術類型 所需周圍環境 自身提供保護
Closed Isolator（封閉隔離器） Grade D Grade A 等效
Open Isolator（開放隔離器） Grade C Grade A 等效
RABS（開放或封閉型） Grade B Grade A
傳統無菌充填 Grade B Grade A（層流）

CDMO 廠房設計含義：選用 Closed Isolator 可以將廠房主體降到 Grade D 等級，大幅降低 HVAC 建造和運營成本。這是許多新建無菌廠選擇 Isolator 的核心財務理由。

重點提示 — Open vs Closed RABS 的差異

雖然 PtC-1 文中未明確區分，但 ISPE 定義如下（參考 PDA PtC-12）：

  • Closed RABS：干預時門始終關閉，只能透過固定手套操作。保護強度較高。
  • Open RABS：允許在特殊情況下打開門進行干預。必須有補充控制措施（煙霧測試、額外消毒、監測等）。

PtC-1 的立場：RABS 開門干預不是禁止的，但必須是「合格干預清單」中預先評估的項目，且附帶明確的額外控制措施。這是一個「風險為本」的方法。

決策框架 — 選擇屏障技術的邏輯樹

新建無菌充填廠房選型決策：

Q1: 產品需要最高無菌保證（高風險、生物製品）？
    → 是：優先考慮 Closed Isolator

Q2: 廠房預算有限，但希望降低環境級別要求？
    → 是：Closed Isolator（Grade D 環境）
    → 否：RABS（Grade B 環境，建造成本較高）

Q3: 產品換型頻繁（CDMO 多產品共線）？
    → 是：RABS 更易於清洗和換型
    → 否：Isolator 去污時間較長，但長期無菌保證更好

Q4: 現有設施升級（改造 Grade B 空間）？
    → RABS 是改造現有潔淨室的理想選擇
    → Isolator 需要更多基礎設施（VHP 系統、廢氣處理）

參考：EU Annex 1 (2022) 明確鼓勵使用 Isolator 或 RABS，
視為對 CCS 的積極貢獻。

實務應用 — CDMO 場景

假設你的 CDMO 同時承接兩個客戶專案：

  • 客戶 A：高價值生物製劑，每批次 500 vials，年產 6 批。要求最高無菌保證，監管機構為 EMA。
  • 客戶 B：通用注射劑，每批次 50,000 vials，年產 50 批，頻繁換型。監管機構為 FDA。

分析：客戶 A 建議使用 Closed Isolator（最高保護，EU 監管傾向）。客戶 B 建議使用 RABS（換型彈性大，批量高）。如果只有一條線，需要做 QRM（品質風險管理）評估共線可行性——這正是 PDA PtC-1 將屏障技術納入 CCS 框架的原因。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 一家工廠將 RABS 設置在 Grade C 環境中，認為已符合 PDA 建議。這樣做是否正確？理由為何？（提示：PtC-1 明確規定 RABS 必須在 Grade B 環境中。）
  2. 當 RABS 需要進行開門干預時，PDA PtC-1 要求的「額外控制措施」至少包含哪幾項？（請列舉至少 4 項。）
  3. Isolator 的內表面被說成是「去污（decontaminated）」而非「滅菌（sterilized）」，這在操作規範上有什麼含義？（提示：手套不能觸碰關鍵表面的原因。）
Topic J: Environmental Clean-Up Period Determination (At Rest) (p27–p28)

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement

How much time is needed to reestablish acceptable cleanroom conditions after disruption of these conditions?

Recommendation

The particle levels for the "at-rest" state should be achieved after a "clean-up period", one that is sufficiently long to allow enough air turnover to return to qualified conditions, that has been established through qualification activities, and is controlled via established procedures.

The best approach for this concept is not a time limit but, rather, a pre-established program of steps and measures to be taken in the event of a deviation in the CCS. This program should not be a description of what to do but, rather, of what to consider when returning an environment to a controlled condition.

Rationale

Cleanroom facilities and operations differ. Therefore, it is impossible to prescribe time limits for reestablishing acceptable cleanroom conditions after a disruption for all facilities and operations. Companies should establish a clean-up period based on system qualification.

"NOTE: EU Annex 1, Section 4.29, does state a guidance value of 20 minutes for cleanroom reestablishment of conditions, but says the time period should be determined under qualification and adhered to in operations."

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — 清除期 (Clean-Up Period)

清除期（Clean-Up Period）是指：潔淨室在受到擾動（例如人員進出、干預操作、設備維修）後，需要多長時間才能恢復到「靜止狀態（At-Rest）」的粒子水準。

PDA PtC-1 的核心立場：清除時間不應是固定的時間規定，而應是透過資格確認（Qualification）建立的、設施專屬的數據。 這反映了 GMP 中「科學為本」的原則——每個廠房的 HVAC 設計、換氣次數（ACH）、房間大小都不同，不可能一刀切。

比喻說明 — 餐廳廚房換氣

想像一個大型廚房在炒菜後充滿油煙：一個小廚房（高換氣率）可能5分鐘後就恢復清潔；一個大型工業廚房（低換氣率、大空間）可能需要30分鐘。你不能規定「所有廚房必須10分鐘清除」——必須實測。

潔淨室也一樣：EU Annex 1 的 20 分鐘是「指引值（guidance value）」，不是強制標準。你的廠房也許 10 分鐘就夠，也許需要 35 分鐘——關鍵是用數據說話。

重點提示 — EU Annex 1 的 20 分鐘與 PDA 立場的差異

EU Annex 1 第 4.29 條：提供 20 分鐘作為指引值，但明確表示應透過資格確認確定具體時間。

PDA PtC-1 立場：更進一步，認為「不應設定時間限制」，而應建立一套「偏差後環境恢復的系統程序」，包括：

  • 確認擾動已停止
  • 驗證 HVAC 運行正常
  • 實際粒子監測確認恢復（而非假設時間到就好）

實務含義：FDA 查核時，查官可能問：「你的清除期是如何確立的？」——你需要提供資格確認的數據，而不只是引用「EU 說 20 分鐘」。

公式參考 — 換氣次數與清除時間的關係

理論清除時間估算（ISPE 方法）：

清除時間 ≈ 3 ÷ ACH（每小時換氣次數）× 60 分鐘

例：Grade B 房間 ACH = 20
→ 理論清除時間 ≈ 3 ÷ 20 × 60 = 9 分鐘（99% 清除率）

但此公式為理論值，實際需透過粒子計數驗證：
- 在擾動後（如人員退出）立即啟動粒子監測
- 記錄粒子數降到 At-Rest 標準的實際時間
- 此時間即為該設施的合格清除期

注意：EU Annex 1 指引值 20 分鐘對應較保守的
換氣次數（~9 ACH），現代潔淨室通常可更快。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 你的工廠 Grade B 填充室的 HVAC 換氣次數為 30 ACH，你的清除期是否可以設定為少於 EU Annex 1 的 20 分鐘指引值？需要提供什麼數據支持？
  2. PDA PtC-1 說清除期「不應是時間限制」，那清除期的觸發條件是什麼？恢復的確認標準又是什麼？
Topic K.1: Blow-Fill-Seal Process Design and Operation (p28–p30)

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement

What are the unique environmental contamination control considerations for the Blow-Fill-Seal (BFS) process?

Recommendation

The environment in which the BFS machine is placed should be sufficient to protect the product-contact surfaces and product from environmental contaminants (typically Grade C). Open drains should not be present in the BFS filling cleanroom.

The critical fill zone environment should be Grade A. This environment can be contained in an enclosed air shroud or barrier, providing that system is qualified and demonstrates a low risk of microbial intrusion.

It should not be necessary to have a Grade B transition area between the Grade A critical zone and the Grade C BFS machine area.

Qualification studies, including airflow visualization studies, should be performed to demonstrate that air from the environment does not flow from the surrounding fill room into the critical fill or exposed parison (transport) areas during operation and during interventions.

The open parison transport environment should meet Grade A conditions and should be controlled and monitored to protect the interior and exterior of the container from contamination during transport. It may be necessary to utilize direct HEPA-filtered airflow over the parison cutting area.

Machinery, equipment, and operations that can be placed outside of the filling room, or otherwise separated from the filling room by way of barriers or BFS line design, should be considered.

Cleanroom personnel performing interventions or otherwise entering the filling room should be gowned for Grade A and Grade B. Any activities in the fill zone must use proper aseptic technique. Interventions should be minimized and limited to those performed outside of the enclosed air-shroud barrier systems and the critical fill and transport zones.

A risk-based approach to EM should be used to select monitoring locations based on areas where environmental contamination poses the greatest risk to product contamination.

"NOTE: For rotary or closed parison BFS machines, it may not be possible to take environmental samples adjacent to the filling nozzle due to the inclusion of the nozzle in the closed parison."

Rationale

A properly designed and operated BFS process may provide a relatively low risk for microbial ingress or contamination of product due to:

  • The high level of automation (no operators in the immediate filling area)
  • Minimal need for interventions
  • Short periods of container exposure to the controlled environment prior to filling and sealing

Due to the design of the BFS process and equipment, it may be difficult to achieve a defined Grade A environment. It may not be possible to achieve correct differential pressures and an adjacent Grade B environment at the extrusion/parison cutting and transport areas. In addition, the parison cutting process may generate airborne particulates. Steps should be taken to examine the transport from the point at which the parison is cut and open to the point at which it enters the enclosed shroud area.

Protection of the open parison during transport and filling should mitigate and control the risk of microbial contamination. Airflow volumes and velocity should be designed and balanced to minimize the risk of ingress of contamination, without creating excessive turbulence or unintentional cooling of the exposed parison, which could result in container formation and seal difficulties.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — BFS 的「先進無菌」地位

Blow-Fill-Seal（BFS，吹瓶-充填-封口）是一種整合式無菌包裝技術：塑膠粒料（Resin）在機器內被加熱擠出成型（Parison，熔融管），同時充填藥液，然後密封——整個過程在幾秒鐘內完成，幾乎沒有「開放暴露」時間。

為何 BFS 不需要 Grade B 過渡區？ 因為 BFS 的核心設計理念是「容器在充填前才存在」——不像傳統玻璃瓶需要運輸、清洗、滅菌等多個步驟，BFS 的容器是「即時製造即時充填」，暴露視窗極短，風險本質上不同。

這是 EU Annex 1（2022）與 FDA 都認可的「特殊情況」，允許 BFS 機房使用 Grade C，但仍要求 Air Shroud 內達到 Grade A 等效。

比喻說明 — BFS 像「現場製作的密封飲料」

傳統無菌充填就像：工廠先生產空玻璃瓶（有清洗、滅菌過程），運到充填室，開口充填，再加蓋。每個步驟都有汙染風險。

BFS 就像：飲料機現場用熱塑膠「吹」出一個杯子，立刻注入飲料，立刻密封。杯子從沒有「空的」狀態——一生出來就被充填了。所以「容器被汙染」的機會視窗幾乎為零。

Air Shroud 就像「機器外罩一層玻璃罩子」，確保這個吹製-充填-密封的瞬間受到 Grade A 潔淨空氣保護。

重點提示 — BFS 的 EM 特殊挑戰

BFS 的環境監測（EM）與傳統充填線不同，有幾個特殊考量：

  • Parison 切割產生粒子：塑膠被切割時會產生顆粒，這些是「非微生物但干擾計數」的粒子。需要建立「基準（Baseline）」來區分製程相關粒子和真正的環境污染。
  • 封閉式 Parison 無法取樣：對於旋轉式或封閉 Parison 設計的 BFS 機器，充填噴嘴在 Parison 內部，根本無法在鄰近位置取 EM 樣本。這是監管機構允許的設計限制，但必須在 EM 計畫中說明理由。
  • Grade A 的認定方式：因 BFS 難以設置標準的 Grade A 差壓環境，監管機構接受「透過資格確認研究（包括煙霧可視化）證明等效 Grade A 保護」的方式。

重點提示 — FDA vs EU Annex 1 對 BFS 的立場對比

FDA（2004 指引）：承認 BFS 的特殊性，接受 Grade C 機房環境，要求 Grade A 等效的關鍵充填區，但沒有明確要求 Grade B 過渡區。

EU Annex 1（2022）：同樣允許 BFS 在 Grade C 操作，明確確認不需要 Grade B 過渡區（這在 2022 年修訂中是一個重要的澄清），但要求充填關鍵區域提供 Grade A 等效保護的書面資格確認。

CDMO 實務：如果同時面向 FDA 和 EMA 市場，BFS 的設計方案通常可以同時滿足兩個監管機構的要求——這是 BFS 的一個監管友好優勢。

實務應用 — BFS CDMO 廠房設計

如果 CDMO 考慮引入一台新的 BFS 機器：

  • 廠房環境：機器主體可在 Grade C，但 Air Shroud 必須設計為 Grade A 等效。
  • 人員更衣：進入 BFS 充填室的人員必須按 Grade A/B 要求更衣（比 Grade C 更嚴格），因為他們一旦進行干預，就是在 Grade A 環境附近操作。
  • EM 計畫：需要特別規劃：哪些位置可取樣、哪些不可取樣（並說明理由）、如何解讀 Parison 切割產生的非生物粒子。
  • APS（無菌製程模擬）：必須模擬 Resin 充填過程，但由於容器為不透明/半透明塑膠，培養基生長的可見性可能受限——需要在 APS 計畫中特別說明判讀方法。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼 PDA PtC-1 說 BFS 機房「不需要 Grade B 過渡區」？這個結論的科學依據是什麼？
  2. BFS 的 Parison 切割區域粒子監測面臨哪些特殊挑戰？廠房應如何處理「因製程產生的非微生物粒子」對監測數據的影響？
Topic K.2: Plastic Resin Storage and Handling (p30–p31)

原文內容 Original Text

Problem Statement

What are the unique container and resin control considerations for the BFS process?

Recommendation

Resin identity and quality should be maintained through the company's approved supply-chain management system. Resin bioburden (including endotoxin) limits should be established, controlled, and monitored based on product requirements.

Resin should be stored and dispensed from a controlled, non-classified area in a manner that prevents the introduction of extraneous contamination. Consideration should be given to temperature and humidity controls.

Resin stored in large refillable containers (i.e., silos) should be monitored for moisture accumulation and bioburden. Such containers should be closed, periodically emptied, and cleaned or sanitized.

Use of a resin-regrind mixture in container formation should be qualified to confirm that such regrind levels are acceptable. Acceptability should be based, at least, on the ability to maintain resin bioburden from the container and the seal of the container, and container integrity should be maintained throughout the shelf life of the product.

Procedures should be established for ensuring clearance and cleaning of current resin from the transport lines and extruder when the changeover of resin is required. Lot traceability of resin and resin-regrind mixture should be maintained.

Rationale

The selection, use, and handling of resin are key components of the BFS process. Resin quality is important to ensure the proper formation, sealing, stability, and overall performance of the containers and the control of bioburden; therefore, resin composition and identity should be maintained. Proper handling and storage should reduce the risk of bioburden formation. Bioburden monitoring should provide additional assurance of resin quality.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — 為什麼 Resin 品質在 BFS 中特別重要？

在傳統無菌充填中，容器（玻璃瓶、安瓿）是預先製造的，廠商通過清洗-去熱原-滅菌來確保無菌。

在 BFS 中，塑膠樹脂（Resin）本身就是容器材料的前驅物。樹脂的微生物負荷（Bioburden）和內毒素（Endotoxin）直接影響最終容器的品質——雖然擠出成型的高溫（通常 >170°C）可殺滅大多數微生物，但高溫不能摧毀內毒素。因此，樹脂的生物負荷管控是 BFS 製程中容易被忽視但至關重要的環節。

重點提示 — Resin Regrind 的使用

Resin Regrind（回收研磨料）是指 BFS 生產中被切除的多餘塑膠（如容器頸部的廢料）被研磨後重新混入新樹脂使用，以減少物料浪費。

PDA PtC-1 的要求：Regrind 的使用必須經過資格確認，至少驗證：

  • 混用比例對生物負荷（Bioburden）的影響
  • 容器封口完整性是否受影響
  • 容器在整個保存期限（Shelf Life）內的完整性

注意：Regrind 在儲存和研磨過程中可能累積微生物，必須監測並設定限值。

重點提示 — Silo（大型儲料倉）的特殊風險
